Jamison Brereton

60 (501)
Indra and Agni
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh 1тАУ3, g─Бyatr─л 4тАУ12, triс╣гс╣нubh 13, br╠еhat─л 14, anuс╣гс╣нubh 15, arranged in trcas ╠е
This Indra-Agni hymn, organized into tr╠еcas, begins with three verses in trimeter meter notable for the tendency to address Indra and Agni separately, each in the vocative singular, though they receive joint epithets, are referred to by shared pro nouns, and are generally, but not exclusively (see vs. 2d), the subjects of dual verbs. Our translation reflects this peculiar disjunction of vocatives. This separate address is not characteristic of the rest of the hymn, where the dual dvandva compound тАЬIndra-AgniтАЭ (or, once, a conjoined phrase тАЬIndra and Agni,тАЭ vs. 12) is found in nine of the remaining twelve verses, and the last tr╠еca begins with a verse (13) con
taining four occurrences of the explicit adjective тАЬ(you) bothтАЭ (ubh─Б╠Б). The content of the praise is generic, with a tendency toward Indraic deeds and qualities (see esp. vss. 3, 6). The second-to-last tr╠еca treats the two gods separately, without naming them: Agni in verse 10, Indra in verse 11, and a return to joint ref erence in verse 12. The final triplet (vss. 13тАУ15) is in three different meters, and it has been suggested that it did not originally belong to the rest of the hymn. However, notice that the return to longer lines matches the meter of the first tr╠еca, and there are also verbal responsions with the first three verses, so that a ring-compositional structure is sketched. The strong emphasis on the unified front presented by the two gods in verses 13тАУ15 contrasts implicitly with the separate address in the first tr╠еca, and may hint that our own hymn has brought about the close cooperation between the two gods that will benefit us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

English translation:

тАЬHe ovecomes his enemy, and acquires food, who worships the victorious Indra and Agni, the lords of infinite opulence, most powerful in strength, desirous of (sacrificial) food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He pierces the obstacle and wins the prize who will serve Indra and Agni, the mighty ones
who have control over abundant goods, the two most mighty with their might as they seek the victory prize.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vocab. of this vs. shows a slight tendency towards morphological elaboration: in addition to the straightforward s├бhastam─Б s├бhas─Б, there is s├бhur─л to the same root but with the rare suffix -uri; the deriv. vasavy├а- for тАШgoodsтАЩ, rather than standard v├бsu (as in the preceding hymn VI.59.9). This latter word returns at the end of the hymn.

The 3rd sg. ┼Ыn├бthat that opens the hymn is somewhat puzzling morphologically.

The root тИЪ┼Ыnath has a poorly attested verbal system, save for the -├бya-transitive and associated redupl. aor.; besides ┼Ыn├бthat it consists only of two exx. of the athem.

impv. ┼Ыnathihi, and a couple of -iс╣г-aor. forms. Narten (258-59) argues convincingly that ┼Ыnathihi should belong to a root aor. (rather than a root pres., as it is generally classed), which could serve as the base for the formation of the -iс╣г-aor. Our form ┼Ыn├бthat could formally easily be a subjunctive to this root aor., but the problem is that a subjunctive works quite badly in context, esp., since it is explicitly conjoined (by ut├б) with the following pres. indic. sanoti. It could alternatively be the injunctive to a them. stem, though in that case it would be the only representative of that stem.

Narten discusses ┼Ыn├бthat in n. 810, where she rather says that though it’s used in a general sense, nothing stands in the way of its being a subj. to the root aor. I find this somewhat disingenuous, as subjunctives arenтАЩt generally (/ever?) used in such a sense. She also allows the possibility that it could be injunctive to a thematic stem.

(see also Klein DGRV I.366, who allows either). Much as I dislike multiplying entities, I’m inclined to go for the thematic injunctive for functional reasons.

Unfortunately a root aor. injunc. *┼Ыnath─лt would have been easy to build, so the thematization cannot be the result of avoiding a problematic form.

Griffith

HE slays the foe and wins the spoil who worships Indra and Agni, strong and mighty Heroes,
Who rule as Sovrans over ample riches, victorious, showing forth their power in conquest.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra and Agni, verily you have combated for (the recovery of) the cows, the waters, the sun, the dawns that had been carried away (by the asuras); you reunite, Indra (with the world), the quarters of the horizon, the sun, the wonderful waters, the dawns, the cattle and so do you, Agni, who have the Niyut steeds.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You two, do battle for cows now, o Indra, for the waters, the sun, and the dawns who were carried (away), o Agni.
The quarters, the sun, the brilliant dawns, o IndraтАФthe waters, the cows, do you, o Agni, as teamster hitch up as your team.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Assuming that uс╣г├бsaс╕е тАж ┼лс╕╖h─Б╠Бс╕е is a single NP, the question is what happened to the dawns. Geldner, fld. by Renou, thinks that the dawns were taken away, that is, abducted (entf├╝hrten, enlev├йes). If, as Geldner suggests (n. 2), this concerns the Vala myth, the dawns qua cows can be conceptualized as taken / stolen by the Paс╣Зis.

(Oberlies [RdV I.180] goes further, seeing this as part of a myth about bridestealing, ultimately involving the A┼Ыvins, though he admits [n. 150] that our vs. does not tell us who abducted the Dawn(s) or where she was taken.) HPS (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 180 n. 33, ) indignantly rejects the abduction interpr. and suggests rather that, on the basis of VI.64.3, 5, the dawns are drawn (┼лс╕╖h─Б╠Бс╕е) by bulls. Although this is possible, and the cited passage is quite nearby, it doesnтАЩt make a lot of sense for Indra and Agni to тАЬdo battleтАЭ for the dawns if the dawns are moving on their own steam, whereas if they were abducted, they need help.

In d Agni must be the immediate subj. of the clause, given the adjacency of the voc. and the 2nd sg. verb (agne yuvase) – but, as Renou points out, niy├║tv─Бn is more an epithet of Indra than of Agni – and, as he doesnтАЩt point out, even more an epithet of V─Бyu in conjunction with Indra. I therefore wonder if this has not been adapted from an Indra-V─Бyu context, with a different set of dual divinities. The d p─Бda is also very close to an Indra passage fairly nearby: VI.47.14 ap├│ g─Б╠Бvajrin yuvase s├бm ├нnd┼лn, with Indra as the subj. of yuvase: тАЬYou join together the waters, the cows, and the drops, you possessor of the mace.тАЭ The substitution of Agni and the attribution to him of IndraтАЩs qualities and actions is in conformity with the tendency noted in the published introduction. of favoring the Indraic in this supposedly shared hymn.

English translation:

тАЬI invoke those two, the whole of whose deeds of old have been celebrated; Indra and Agni harm us not.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I call upon these two whose every previous deed is admired.
Indra and Agni do not neglect (us).

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not have a view on how (or whether) to fix the meter of p─Бda a; see Oldenberg

It is thinkable, but by no means necessary, that instead of reading quadrisyllabic ├нndr─Б-agn─л (as in vss. 5, 7, 14), we could read trisyllabic ├нndr─Бgn─л (as in 8, 9, 15) with a haplologized enclitic naс╕е: ├нndr─Бgn─л n├б *no mardhataс╕е.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the phonological (and partly etymological) figure mardh(ataс╕е) (4c), mс╣Ы╠Бdh(aс╕е) (5a), mс╣Ыс╕╖(─Бtaс╕е) (5c).

Griffith

I call the Twain whose deeds of old have all been famed in ancient days
O Indra-Agni, harm us not.

Geldner

Die beiden rufe ich, von denen alles das, was sie vormals taten, Anerkennung findet. Indra und Agni lassen nicht im Stich.

Grassmann

Die ruf’ ich, deren ganze Welt, die sie geschaffen, herrlich ist, Nie werden Indra-Agni matt.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬCounteract all oppressions (committed) by the pious; counteract all oppressions (committed) by the impious; protectors of the virtuous, destroy all those who hate us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Hato vс╣Ыtr─Бс╣Зi ─Бry─Б hasto d─Бs─Бni: vс╣Ыtr─Бс╣Зi and d─Бs─Бni are neuter and may not signify ─Бryas and d─Бsas themselves; so, the interpretation is: ─Бryaiс╕е and d─Бsaiс╕е kс╣Ыt─Бni, things done by them severally, that is, upadravaj─Бt─Бni, things genitive rated by violence or oppression and the like. This is a remarkable equivalence between ─Бryas and d─Бsas

Jamison Brereton

They smash the ─Аrya obstacles; they smash those of the D─БsaтАФthe two lords of settlements;
they smash away all hatreds.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the curious position of ├бpa in tmesis, embedded in the obj. NP: hat├│ v├н┼Ыv─Б ├бpa dv├нс╣гaс╕е.

And drive our enemies away.

English translation:

тАЬIndra and Agni, leaders (of rites), whose Niyut steeds are desired by many, come with them to the donor (of the libation).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Those much-sought-after teams of yours which are for the pious, you superior men,
come here with those, o Indra and Agni.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I follow Geldner in construing d─Б┼Ы├║с╣гe with s├бnti (тАЬwhich are for the piousтАЭ) rather than with puruspс╣Ы╠Бhaс╕е (Renou тАЬpour lтАЩadorateur les tr├иs envi├йsтАЭ) because puruspс╣Ы╠Бh- doesnтАЩt seem to appear with a dat. elsewhere. See the almost identical IV.47.4.

English translation:

тАЬGlorify that Agni who envelopes all the forest with flame, who blackens them with (his) tongue.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Reverently invoke him who with his flame embraces all the trees, who makes them black with his tongue.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The root тИЪsva├▒j is ordinarily middle; it has only two active forms, this one (pariс╣гv├бjat) and the plupf. pary├бс╣гasvajat in I.182.7. The latter can be explained as an ├бduhat-type remarking of the middle pf. с╣гasvaje (see comm. ad loc.), but this active remarking of the them. pres. -с╣гv├бjate is harder to explain. Got┼Н (1st Kl., 338-39) notes the prevailing middle voice and this anomalous act., but makes no attempt to account for it.

Griffith

Glorify him who compasses all forests with his glowing flame,
And leaves them blackened with his tongue.

English translation:

тАЬThe mortal who presents the gratifying (oblation) to Indra in the kindled (fire), to him (Indra grants) acceptable waters for his sustenance.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The mortal who, when (the ritual fire) has been kindled, seeks to win the favor of Indra,
(for him Indra makes) the waters easy to cross for brilliance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntactic affiliation of the final p─Бda of this vs., consisting of a dat. dyumn─Б╠Бya and an acc. phrase sut├бr─Б ap├бс╕е, is unclear. Oldenberg suggests taking the acc. as a second obj. of ─Бv├нv─Бsati, or rather suggests supplying the same verb as main clause verb тАЬ(he also wins) waters тАжтАЭ But since the structure of ab, in which the mortal seeks IndraтАЩs favor, invites a demonstration of that favor in the main cl., I therefore borrow kс╣Ыс╣Зoti (deaccented) from 10c, with Indra as subj. This is also RenouтАЩs solution and apparently GeldnerтАЩs. For тИЪkс╣Ы in similar expressions, see VII.97.8 k├бrad br├бhmaс╣Зe sut├бr─Б sug─Бdh─Б╠Б тАЬHe [=Bс╣Ыhaspati/Indra] will make good fords, easy to cross, for the sacred formulationтАЭ and IV.19.6 sutaraс╣З─Б╠Бm akс╣Ыс╣Зor indra s├нndh┼лn тАЬYou made the rivers easy to cross, Indra.тАЭ

Griffith

He who gains Indra’s bliss with fire enkindled finds an easy way
Over the floods to happiness.

Geldner

Welcher Sterbliche bei entflammtem Feuer die Gunst des Indra erbittet, dem machet ihr zum Ruhmglanze die Gew├дsser leicht ├╝berschreitbar.

Grassmann

Der Sterbliche, der Indra’s Huld bei Agni’s Flamme sich gewinnt, Der dringt durch Fluten schnell zum Heil.

Elizarenkova

тАЬMay those two grant us strengthening food, and swift horses to convey (our offerings).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You two, deliver to us refreshments accompanied by prizes, and deliver (to safety) swift steeds
to convey Indra and Agni.

Abundant strengthening food on us.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI invoke you both, Indra and Agni, to be present at the sacrifice; and both together to be exhilarated by the (sacrificial) food; for you are both donors of food and riches, and therefore I invoke you both for the obtaining of sustenance.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You both, Indra and Agni, are to be called upon; both together are to invigorate yourselves on bounty.
You both are givers of refreshments, of riches; you both do I call upon to win the victory prize.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the insistent ubh─Б╠Бsee published introduction.

I have taken ─Бhuv├бdhyai (and m─Бday├бdhyai) as predicated infinitives with the subj. ubh─Б╠Б, as does Renou However, v─Бm in p─Бda a makes some difficulties for this interpr., and Geldner takes that p─Бda (but not b) as having an implicit 1st ps. subj.: тАЬeuch beide тАж will ich herrufenтАЭ (a) versus тАЬbeiden sollen sich тАж erfreuenтАЭ for m─Бday├бdhyai (b). I think the two clauses should be parallel and therefore take v─Бm as a dependent gen. on ubh─Б╠Б(тАЬboth of you twoтАЭ), although it must be admitted that ubh├б- generally agrees with its referent in case.

Griffith

Indra and Agni, I will call you hither and make you joyful with the gifts I offer.
Ye Twain are givers both of food and riches: to win me strength and vigour I invoke you.

Keith

Ye twain shall be summoned, O Indra and Agni.
Ye twain shall rejoice together in the offering.
You both givers of food and riches,
You both I summon for the winning of strength.

Euch beide, Indra und Agni, will ich herrufen; beide sollen sich zusammen der Opfergaben erfreuen. Beide sind die Geber von Speisegen├╝ssen, von Reicht├╝mern; euch beide rufe ich, um den Lohn zu gewinnen.
